  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4e4675af-49cf-44ba-8611-7840ae11bc0a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/291569-okay-so-after-looking-at-the-different">Okay, so after looking at the different books in The Selection Series, I&#39;m confused about which book I should start with. Do I start with The Prince and work my way through the series according to the numbers? 0.5 implies that it was published after The Selection but is talking about events that happened before it. . . Anyways, I&#39;m confused. To the fans out there, in what order should I read the books?</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This is the order that I read them in (that way you don't spoil anything for yourself and the content of the novella is still relevant to where you ar<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This is the order that I read them in (that way you don't spoil anything for yourself and the content of the novella is still relevant to where you are in the series):<br /><br />The Selection<br />The Elite<br />The Prince<br />The Guard<br />The One<br />The Queen<br />The Favorite<br />Happily Ever After (for the extra scenes aside from the novellas)<br />The Heir<br />The Crown<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11456033-karla?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662242318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9011037157246296849"><b>AFTER READ:</b><br/><br/>Oh man, this was a painful thing to read. Aspen whined and minimized Maxon's character and feelings for the whole time up until the last few pages.<br/><br/>Hard to understand someone's point of view when all they want is the girl, not considering that maybe he's risking her life.<br/><br/>URGH.<br/><br/><b>BEFORE READ:</b><br/><br/>I will not be swayed, Kiera Cass.<br/><br/>Maxon is my forever boy.<br/><br/>(But I'll probably read this anyways).</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_711735213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/711735213" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/711735213?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=disappointments">disappointments</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer711735213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13425321803664279237"><b> Please excuse this fangirl-is-angry-don't-mess-with-her rant. </b><br/><br/>I seriously don't know where to start with this novella. Honestly, it just made me VERY mad. First of all, everyone says "You're Team Maxon right?" Of course I am!! There is no Team Aspen. There's either Team Maxon or there's Team NOT Maxon. No one actually likes Aspen. He's just a self-centered guy who's cocky and arrogant and only cares about himself and his family. Throughout this book he always thinks that he's 100% correct about</span>
  <span id="freeText13425321803664279237" style="display:none"><b> Please excuse this fangirl-is-angry-don't-mess-with-her rant. </b><br /><br />I seriously don't know where to start with this novella. Honestly, it just made me VERY mad. First of all, everyone says "You're Team Maxon right?" Of course I am!! There is no Team Aspen. There's either Team Maxon or there's Team NOT Maxon. No one actually likes Aspen. He's just a self-centered guy who's cocky and arrogant and only cares about himself and his family. Throughout this book he always thinks that he's 100% correct about everything. And everyone in the palace fawning over him and saying what a bright star he is doesn't help shrink his huge ego any bit. He has rigid opinions on everything and refuses to be swayed. It's ridiculous. HE'S ridiculous. How America likes him or what she sees in him I will never know. Then again, America Singer isn't the brightest girl on the block. I despised her in "The Elite" and even more so in this novella. Aspen is badmouthing Maxon, and America does nothing!! She doesn't defend Maxon or tell Aspen that he's wrong about Maxon. She just agrees with whatever Aspen says and takes it like it's the freaking word of God. And Aspen calls Maxon an actor and says that he's actually a really bad person (takes one to know one), I was just thinking, I DON'T CARE WHAT YOU THINK ASPEN LEGER. I DON'T CARE. GET OFF THE BOOK'S PAGES AND GIVE ME MAXON!! And America keeps messing around with Aspen behind Maxon's back?! That is so low, and does she not remember what just happened to her friend Marlee?! Talk about inconsiderate and stupid and foolish. And Aspen, he claims that he loves her yet he's putting her in so much danger by pursuing her. If Aspen really loved her, he'd let her go. But he won't because he is a selfish adolescent who wants everything. If I hear Aspen call America "my girl" one more time I might just reach into the book and slap him so hard he sees stars. She is NOT your girl. You dumped her and now you want her back when she's suddenly all rich and high caste and famous?! Aspen is really naive and foolish if he can't see the sparks between America and Maxon. Stop. Pining. Over. America. I also love how Aspen talks about Maxon like he knows Maxon so well, like their best buds and that Aspen knows everything about Maxon. No he does not!! They haven't even spoken two words to each other!! I feel as though Kiera Cass has tried and failed to turn people over to Team Aspen, and she failed to make people think that Aspen's great, because he's not. Cass basically just threw Aspen at us and said "Hey!! Like him!! He's wonderful!! I just realized that I created the weakest love triangle in existence of any YA series so I'm gonna make it up to my readers now by giving the illusion of a strong love triangle since my series has nothing else to offer." Aspen's POV was so dull and boring, and I just hate him so much. I was begging for just one or two lines from my dearest Maxon. My brain can only take Aspen's stupidity and self-righteousness for so long.<br /><br />Well I'd like to apologize for whatever I just wrote. I am fed up. *crosses arms and taps foot*<br /><br />I am SO excited for <i> The One </i> though!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13425321803664279237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047721364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10067514168144038223"><u>3 Time was the ONLY thing ★'s</u> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Any girl who would risk her life for someone she loves certainly deserves to be called a lady.”</i>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>
  <i>“Accepting help is its own kind of strength”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Buddy read with my, girl <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/86233338-desire-lambert' rel='nofollow noopener'>Desireé</a> :) <br/><br/><i>The Guard</i> novella was... Well, it was just an okay read I guess. I get a bit bored when novella's repeat parts from previous books. And if I'm being honest Aspen's POV really didn't add that much to the story which is sad because I was looking most forward to his. I guess I was looking</span>
  <span id="freeText10067514168144038223" style="display:none"><u>3 Time was the ONLY thing ★'s</u> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Any girl who would risk her life for someone she loves certainly deserves to be called a lady.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“Accepting help is its own kind of strength”</i>
</b><br><br>Buddy read with my, girl <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/86233338-desire-lambert" rel="nofollow noopener">Desireé</a> :) <br><br><i>The Guard</i> novella was... Well, it was just an okay read I guess. I get a bit bored when novella's repeat parts from previous books. And if I'm being honest Aspen's POV really didn't add that much to the story which is sad because I was looking most forward to his. I guess I was looking for something more and sadly this just didn't deliver. On the other hand, this was a very quick and easy read. And though I distaste repeated scenes (scenes from book 2) it was still nice getting a look into his thoughts and feelings and his desires. Aspens POV gives us insight into King Clarkson's nature, motivations, manipulative ways, and his cruelty. It was also nice getting to see the relationship's form between him and America's maids Anne, Mary and Lucy and the respect they have for him and the love they have for America. It was nice seeing Aspen's camaraderie with the other guards, especially with Avery and Tanner. Also, I enjoyed the couple scenes between Aspen and the old man who works in the stables. The old man gives some pretty good advice too :) My rating for this book has nothing to do with my liking or not liking Aspen. It's solely based on the content and the entertainment factor which was very low in my opinion. And... For the record, I have always loved Aspen ever since the first book! Not necessarily with America but because his dedication to America remains steadfast throughout EVERYTHING and he's caring, sweet and all around a wonderful person. Moving on to <i>The Favorite</i> :) <br><br>Illustration of Aspen &amp; What I picture he'd look like.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544243935i/26712472.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“I stored up every moment like it was a physical thing. I'd thumb through memories whenever things were still. I spent more time with her than she ever knew.” </i><br><br><i>“I pushed my lips to hers, locking her to me with a hand knotted into her hair. Stupid. So, so stupid. But right in a thousand ways. It felt like an eternity had passed since we'd kissed this deeply, but we fell into it so easily.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543991333ra/26692646.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“You’re the only thing I’ve ever wanted to fight for.”</i></span>

<div id="review_1710331338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1710331338" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1710331338?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51318038-elena?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1710331338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5390754837211113674"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Any girl who would risk her life for someone she loves certainly deserves to be called a lady.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I've said this before and since the series kept going, I didn't stop: <b>I never liked Aspen.</b> It's not surprising since he is one of the most hated characters simply because he would get in America's way and would ruin her relationship with Maxon. I didn't like him in Book 1 and continued disliking him until book 4. Finding out he wasn't in <i>The Crown,</i> I was happy, glad and cheerful. I honestly wonder</span>
  <span id="freeText5390754837211113674" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>❝Any girl who would risk her life for someone she loves certainly deserves to be called a lady.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />I've said this before and since the series kept going, I didn't stop: <b>I never liked Aspen.</b> It's not surprising since he is one of the most hated characters simply because he would get in America's way and would ruin her relationship with Maxon. I didn't like him in Book 1 and continued disliking him until book 4. Finding out he wasn't in <i>The Crown,</i> I was happy, glad and cheerful. I honestly wonder why, just out of curiosity. I didn't feel any connections toward him and I was glad America was slowly making up her mind and choosing Maxon instead of Aspen. He was cute in the beginning because of his little moments with America. The sad thing is, he wasn't even able to be open about it. If he was a little open and maybe admitted his love for America to her parents or someone related, things would change. But he wanted it to be kept a secret like America. America is different though—she's the girl. If he stepped up and made an actual move, maybe I would think differently of him.<br /><br />He was a jerk to America and continued to be. Reading from his point of view didn't change much. In fact, it didn't change anything. I've never liked him and glad I never did, glad I never shipped him and America. I was Team Maxon since the very beginning until the end. At least he ended up getting another girlfriend and everything worked out between them. Luckily, America approved his relationship with Lucy and at least they got married.<br /><br />I know my thoughts about Aspen would be bad since the beginning. When I felt a connection between America and Maxon, Aspen was just in the way. I didn't feel anything for him and would constantly ask myself why he was in the series after all. I get the beginning, but why until book 4. Even though he married Lucy, I still didn't like him at all. I don't know what's wrong with me. He always got in the way and would end up confusing America, leaving her thinking if she's still in love with him or with Maxon and all I wanted was for both to make up their minds.<br /><br />I was glad this wasn't just another love story and tell us more about how America and Aspen really controlled their relationship in the past and how everything was working out, but instead it delivered events from <i>The Elite.</i> I was actually glad since I couldn't stand moments of Aspen, I wouldn't be able to stand moments between America and Aspen <i>told in his point of view.</i> Again, nothing was new and interesting and his feelings for America didn't change. He cared about her constantly and would be missing her, while I was over here reading the novella, growing tired and bored from it.<br /><br />Understanding his character now doesn't make much of a difference. I wish Kiera provided more information about him in The Selection but also drop him off when he <i>broke</i> America's heart. Even though he is the one to blame for America entering the competition, I guess he is the one to thank her for that. Can't remember if America ever did thank him for that since he is the one who convinced her because he kept telling her she could be fed food she never thought she'd be eating and would be living a life she never imagined, when Aspen would have to take care of his family and her at the same time, not being able to provide enough food and meals for everyone and not being able to make her happy. Even though America didn't care much about that, she thought she knew she would always be with Aspen and their relationship would work out, everything would settle and they would both be happy, I knew they would have to split at some point since the series focuses on America and Maxon.<br /><br />I don't see how a short story told in his view was really needed. It's much different than Maxon's and Aspen's didn't even feel needed and right. I wish we got more stories told from other characters point of views, maybe learn some history and the past from someone else. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5390754837211113674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_857459166" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857459166" />
    <a title="Hannah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17980375-hannah"><img alt="Hannah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424045869p2/17980375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/857459166?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah" href="/user/show/17980375-hannah">Hannah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17980375-hannah?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17980375-hannah?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857459166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4852290559982861202">Okay, I'm just being honest here but this novella pissed me off so much I couldn't even finish it. This is going to turn into a huge rant.<br/><br/>First of all, how does Aspen figure that he knows Maxon so well? How does he know that he's this horrible guy who just pretends to be decent and caring? Has he ever actually spoken to him? Has he ever made an attempt to know him? All Aspen does is make assumptions. He assumes America still loves him, he assumes Maxon is mistreating America when he never consid</span>
  <span id="freeText4852290559982861202" style="display:none">Okay, I'm just being honest here but this novella pissed me off so much I couldn't even finish it. This is going to turn into a huge rant.<br /><br />First of all, how does Aspen figure that he knows Maxon so well? How does he know that he's this horrible guy who just pretends to be decent and caring? Has he ever actually spoken to him? Has he ever made an attempt to know him? All Aspen does is make assumptions. He assumes America still loves him, he assumes Maxon is mistreating America when he never considers for one second what Maxon's life must be like. He never wants to see any good side to Maxon. It's so infuriating and Aspen thinks so highly of himself. Oh he's the best guard and the best person and he's so great yea no, you're not. You say that of all people Maxon is mistreating America when you are the one who is constantly and selfishly putting her in danger because you cant keep your hormones in check? It absolutely boggles my mind how sure he is that they wont get caught, he doesn't even give it a second thought really. Is he considering what could happen if they were caught? No. He's only thinking about himself and what he wants. <br /><br />I never liked Aspen but this novella made me want to ring his damn neck. What a pompous self obsessed jerk off. Every time he called American <i>my girl</i> I wanted to punch him in the mouth. No dude, she's not your girl. She's not in love with you anymore. It pissed me off in The Elite when America just believes everything Aspen says about Maxon when there is zero evidence, when she has had no reason to doubt his intentions. Like Aspen is the expert on Maxon, considering he's spent so much time with him right? Having to relive that moment in this thing just pushed me too far. I cant listen to him bad mouth Maxon when he doesn't have any idea what he's talking about and I cant stand America just sitting there agreeing with him. It makes me think America doesn't even deserve Maxon, because he's been nothing but kind and noble and supportive. I have to remember how America changed her tune at the end of The Elite. It better stay that way because if she becomes indecisive again and goes back to Aspen at all during The One I might lose my mind and chuck the book out of my moving car. <br /><br />On the plus side I did really enjoy the excerpt from The One. It was so funny how America was trying to be all sexy and seduce Maxon and he knew it. Oh man, if the whole book is filled with moments like that then I will thoroughly enjoy it. America seems very sure that she wants him, and I hope that never wavers because I cant take any more of this weak ass love triangle. Oh another thing this about this novella is that is further cemented by belief that America's father is a rebel. I think I'm done ranting now, but I really wish Aspen would get bitch slapped because he's the most arrogant character I've ever read about. It's not even that he's a horrible person in general, I mean he protects his family and everything and he cares about America but dear god, he is a real jerk and he assumes to know what's best for America and thinks he has to convince her of what he thinks she should do rather than letting her figure it out for herself. Which is what Maxon has done, he's given America time and space and everything she's needed. I don't see how America could end up with Aspen at all. It wouldn't make sense for the characters or the series as a whole. I kind of feel bad giving this one star, the writing isn't bad but considering I couldn't even finish it because Aspen was so infuriating I don't think I can give it any more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4852290559982861202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer866163988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10852165301166201380">'The Guard' was a great addition to the series. Before reading this book, I wasn't sure what to think of Aspen at all. Was he the philandering, lying ex-boyfriend that didn't want America but couldn't stand the thought of her being happy with somebody else's? Or, had his love for America been so strong that he sacrificed his own desires to offer her a chance at a better life, one that he knew he couldn't ever offer her? Seeing events unfold through his eyes answered any questions I had about his</span>
  <span id="freeText10852165301166201380" style="display:none">'The Guard' was a great addition to the series. Before reading this book, I wasn't sure what to think of Aspen at all. Was he the philandering, lying ex-boyfriend that didn't want America but couldn't stand the thought of her being happy with somebody else's? Or, had his love for America been so strong that he sacrificed his own desires to offer her a chance at a better life, one that he knew he couldn't ever offer her? Seeing events unfold through his eyes answered any questions I had about his true nature.<br /><br />As a guard, Aspen's perspective also provides valuable insights about the King's nature and motivations. He silently witnesses the King's cruel and manipulative ways and his loyalty is put to the test.<br /><br />His dedication to America remains steadfast. He is determined to win her back, now realizing that pushing her to enter the lottery might have been the biggest mistake of his life. As she struggles with her feelings for the two men, Aspen offers her the emotional support she needs, while trying to keep her from losing touch with her former self.<br /><br />This was a quick and easy read, that I would recommend to anyone who has enjoyed this series. Aspen's story is heartbreakingly sweet as he does everything within his power to support the girl he loves, as he watches her fall for someone else. I'm really glad his side of the story was written. I like Aspen so much more now, having read his perspective.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10852165301166201380" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8352032497367766298" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE REVIEW: </b> I LOVE LOVE THIS BOOK. I was actually for reading about Aspen's point of view of what is happening around palace. First of all, I got know Aspen more then I thought reading the selection series. Aspen Ledger strikes me as a guy that he thinks he has to carry the world's problem in his shoulders. He truly cares about the people around him and tries to help out people when he can. He tried to send some money to Carter Woodwork's mother and I thought it was sweet of him. I got to say fall in love with Aspen more and more as I read this book. Not only that it explains how things go around the palace but we found out the evil ways of the king. Now, i dislike him very much. Maxon, I think you need to open your eyes a little bit, I love love you too but you need to land a punch on your father but he is a big meanie. But anyways, I finally got the reason why he let go of America when they were at the tree house. All he wanted is to give her the world and he thought that by getting her in the selection would give her a better life. Overall Aspen Ledger is a kind hearted, loving, protective and he has motivates for the things that he say or do when he's around America. I mean, sure sometimes we don't like it but hey! he really loves America and all he wanted is her back and what is good for her. My heart ache a little just writing his review. <br /><br />Also does anyone notice that maybe Lucy is crushing on Aspen? Because when America (does) end up with Maxon. I don't mind shipping Lucy and Aspen. I think it's cute.<br /><br />Also just reading this book made me realize that I can't hate Aspen. I'm a big fan of Maxon and both guys is really good for America. I mean I don't know who I would pick but I'm happy either way. <br /><br /> Job well Kiera Cass! I've always been a fan of your work (: <br /><br />2013: Regardless that Aspen can be a pain in someways. He still have a a place in my heart and that I wanted to see what he thinks about this. He does love America and he made a mistake when he push her away. But I still like him but not much as Maxon but I will definitely read this book (: </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=really-liked-it">really-liked-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=romance-lovey-dovey">romance-lovey-dovey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=read-always-one-author-challenge">read-always-one-author-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/55299343-fuzaila?shelf=spin-offs">spin-offs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075416432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3779336452722326114"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> "We know you are strong, but accepting help is its own kind of strength.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>This book was soo good! </b>I have no idea why or how Kiera Cass manages to utterly disappoint me with a book, and then wow me with the other. She really is a kind of her own making.<br/><br/><b>The Guard</b> is an insight into the tough life of Aspen as the palace guard. His take on the whole Selection process and hearing his side of the story was very refreshingly beautiful. His endless passion for all things is obvious. I loved </span>
  <span id="freeText3779336452722326114" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> "We know you are strong, but accepting help is its own kind of strength.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>This book was soo good! </b>I have no idea why or how Kiera Cass manages to utterly disappoint me with a book, and then wow me with the other. She really is a kind of her own making.<br /><br /><b>The Guard</b> is an insight into the tough life of Aspen as the palace guard. His take on the whole Selection process and hearing his side of the story was very refreshingly beautiful. His endless passion for all things is obvious. I loved the way he analyzed things in his own way, even if he wasn’t always right. Like, what he thought of King Clarkson -<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Of course the man with everything he could ever need or want didn’t understand why any average person might want the same chance”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Or about America’s dad – <br /><blockquote><b><i>'Out of the millions of words in the world, Mr. Singer always seemed to know how to pick the handful that made you feel like you mattered.’</i></b> </blockquote><br /><br />That’s so very true! (As was seen in Mr. Singer’s letters to America) <br /><br />I was stunned to see how perfectly Kiera Cass has worded each feeling and thoughts, and made them unbelievably real. This book was so<u> beautifully written,</u> I am slapping myself for ever doubting Cass’s mastery of words. She has this simple, lyrical prose, and yet she manages to hold so much depth and emotions in the very handful of the words she uses.<br /><br />There was one thing I noticed though, like this – <br /><i>I swear, I wanted to give my girl a medal.’</i> I mean, what is there to swear about? Such sentences were a bit repetitive. Not that I mind them :)<br /><br />Through this book, I’ve also learned much more of the setting of The Selection. The rebel attacks as seen through the eyes of Aspen differ so much from America’s pov. Hearing about them from America sitting in a safe room wasn’t all that informative it seems!<br /><br />I also was wondering how Aspen and Lucy became close, or how they could ever be a good match for each other – but this book has vanquished such doubts too. I can see for myself now, that they were meant to be.<br /><br />Only problem with this book? Well, I really wished it was a bit longer. There were so many things I would have loved to see through Aspen’s eyes. Like, the end of the selection, America and Aspen’s marriage, or his reaction when he finds Marlee and Carter were still in the palace. Nevertheless, I can’t complain. It was just really good. <b>4.5/5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3779336452722326114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17602549174383007782" style="display:none">*Huge Sighs*<br /><br />When I first started reading this series, I instantly fell in love with the entire story line, the whole idea of what Kiera Cass had created with her magical way of writing...<br /><br />I immediately fell in love with Aspen and Mer (America) and I wasn't sure about Prince Maxon. As the story progressed and the books fell away from my hands, my heart changed it's way of thinking... Aspen still clung to me but Maxon surprisingly grew to be something else and I began to fall....<br /><br />Having read The Guard and seen things from Aspen's point of view, my heart has reclaimed him and his love for Mer, I can't stand by and deny this any longer.<br /><br />What is even more interesting is the rumours and the sights that Aspen see's as a Guard and now I know there is something else going on, as we did before but now it's quite plain to see and feel. Whether Maxon is a part of this 'something' or has his own motives for his own 'something' remains to be seen.<br /><br />The new book is on the horizon so it is with great pleasure that I am going to partake in a 'Buddy Re-Read' of this magical series before I embark on the final journey...<br /><br />Team Aspen!!!!<br /><br />I truly love these books!!! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12973944425265463351">It’s not a secret that I am not an Aspen fan. To me, he always seemed so…unnecesary? Is that the right word? I don’t know. He’s just so, bland, I guess.<br/><br/>He dumps the girl he loves, tells her to go and join the selection and marry the prince, and then acts hella petty when she does it. And then he refuses to let her go! Like, boy, could you not. Could you really, really not.<br/><br/>Seeing things from Aspen’s POV was alright, I suppose. I just felt like it was unimportant.   <span id="freeText12973944425265463351" style="display:none">It’s not a secret that I am not an Aspen fan. To me, he always seemed so…unnecesary? Is that the right word? I don’t know. He’s just so, bland, I guess.<br /><br />He dumps the girl he loves, tells her to go and join the selection and marry the prince, and then acts hella petty when she does it. And then he refuses to let her go! Like, boy, could you not. Could you really, really not.<br /><br />Seeing things from Aspen’s POV was alright, I suppose. I just felt like it was unimportant. At least with The Queen, we got to know a new character and saw a different selection. We also got to see a kinder King Clarkson and his relationship with Queen Amberly. With The Prince, we got to learn something different also. We see how a bit of Clarkson’s and Maxon’s relationship. We see how Maxon first reacted to America and how their relationship began. With The Guard we got, what? Just aspen being moody and hating on Maxon. We learned nothing. Honestly, I was just bored.<br /><br />This isn’t really a review. It’s basically just me hating on Aspen. He should have just let America go, focused on his family and left it all alone.<br /><br />Well, I guess this review is done now.<br /><br />Team Maxon all the way!</span>

        <a title="TJ *Book Twins Reviews*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TJ *Book Twins Reviews*" href="/user/show/33488158-tj-book-twins-reviews">TJ *Book Twins Reviews*</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2092484677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9967179132246389606">3.5 Stars <br/><br/>This is a decent supplement to The Selection story. It's an inside look into Aspen's thoughts about America during the events of Book 2. Perhaps I would have enjoyed this more if I'd read the stories in sequence, however it didn't pack as big a punch since I've completed the entire series. Diehard fans of the series will enjoy the additional insight.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3299978302" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3299978302" />
    <a title="Ani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36018660-ani"><img alt="Ani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605390199p2/36018660.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3299978302?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ani" href="/user/show/36018660-ani">Ani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3299978302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18153608825697471269">Wow. I think that, of the 3 novellas I already read, this was by far the most entertaining one. It wasn't funny or anything great, but it was entertaining enough and centered enough to make me like it. And I don't even like Aspen.<br/>But it was great seeing things from his side. I thought I'd be annoyed by his thoughts and actions, but if anything, it actually made me like him for the first time.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sGiz3KXmRwNsBR+dlLUP8oLkWVZE5pF0vREdd6f4F+r75x+EhiUtOtfrlmabLR1jsjmY6ObfYCXHV7TjC0HwiA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vwnpG/HXYAoQs1xuhyKYqm78Qw545BpOe7ZL7nY02VH0hkVD0hQKM6td1ZWIuoo7XiGCsNrd6x8B8OJ62o0+Mw==')})
  }
//]]>

Style. Soda. Spending an hour typing at a coffee shop. Musicals. Back to school season. Mopeds. Good hair days. Naps. Not walking up but looking at a beautiful staircase. Driving alone. My ankles. Playlists. Spending entire days in pajamas. Holidays. Telling stories. Spontaneity. Theme parks. Bookshelves. The word copacetic. Boxes. Empty journals. Surprises. Doing things in groups. Doing things alone. Getting real mail. Decorating. Small forks. A good hug. Gift cards. New Years Goals. Going out to dinner. When someone else remembers some great story about me/us that I’ve forgotten. Toy stores. Fireplaces. Breakfast foods. Journaling. Crying for a good reason. Doorbells. Pointless adventures. Voting. My birthday. Reasons to make wishes. Recycling.<br /></span>
